SUMMARY OF NPC TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE (TA) COMPONENT
1.     ADB Funded Technical Assistance
(1)    Institutional Support - Accounting Services (US$1.2million)
This project will review NPC's present accounting system, and its planned restructuring and privatization
program, and recommend an accounting system which will be appropriate to its needs. The project will (i) design
a management information system and accounting system which is appropriate to the needs of the holding
company and subsidiaries; (ii) recommend the extent of centralization that is justified for the accounting services;
(iii) develop a uniform code of accounts for the holding company and subsidiaries; (iv) develop standardized
accounting manuals for the holding company and subsidiaries; (v) monitor the implementation of the accounting
systems; and (vi) train staff in the implementation and maintenance of the management information system and
accounting system;
(ii)   Institutional Support - Human Resources/Change Management (US$200,000)
The restructuring and privatization of NPC will require changes to its organization and use of human resources.
This will require the transfer of some personnel to subsidiaries, and may have to be accompanied by training to
impart new skills. The privatization exercise will lead to an optimization of its present human resources, and may
require reduction in staff. In the latter case, plans must be prepared to assist affected persons in obtaining gainful
employment. Assistance is to be provided in (i) drafting a policy statement on the principles and goals to retain
staff; (ii) determining staffing requirements after taking into consideration practices in similar utilities and the
need to avoid duplication; (iii) preparing a master plan for human resource deployment and the associated
training needs; (iv) determining remuneration levels; (v) determining mechanisms for the preservation of rights
and benefits of persons transferring to subsidiaries; (vi) establishing guidelines for an employee stock ownership
scheme; and (vii) recommending a system for human resource record keeping;
(iii)   Institutional Support - Valuation of Plant in Service (US$1.3 million)
Covenants with multilateral lending institutions require NPC to perform a full-scale valuation of its plant in
service every 4 years. The last full valuation was performed in 1992 therefore another valuation is due in 1996.
The 1992 valuation concentrated on power plants. Work on transmission assets was limited and no valuation
was performed for buildings. Since up to date valuations have a direct bearing on the valuation of a subsidiary's
equity, it is important that these values be correct. The valuation must also be suitable for establishing the rate
bas of each company, and must be acceptable to regulatory bodies and the Security and Exchange Commission.
The work to be performed would include (i) valuation of production plants; (ii) valuation of each transmission
line 69 kV or higher in areas served by NPC; (iii) valuation of each substation and switching station in the NPC
system; (iv) valuation of all NPC owned buildings; and (v) ensuring that values have been correctly recorded in
the books of account.
(iv)   Institutional Support - Wheeling Tariffs (US$l150000)
Initially the transmission subsidiary company (TRANSCO) will have to face high operating costs attributable to
the 69kV sub-transmission systems which represent over 70% of the circuit length of all transmission lines. It is
expected that a substantial part of the 69kV systems will eventually be transferred to distribution utilities. A
mechanism is needed to demonstrate transparently that wheeling tariffs to be charged by TRANSCO cover only
its cost and a fair return. Assistance is needed to (i) develop a transparent mechanism to calculate wheeling
charges; (ii) design a financial model to facilitate transparent calculations of tariffs which is suited to changing
conditions; and (iii) develop adequate programs to calculate load flows and losses, and a dispatch system that can
record all parameters pertinent to costs.



-85 -                                      Annex 17
Paze 2 of 5
(v)    Institutional Support - Tools for Financial Evaluations (US$25.000)
Assistance is needed in the development of a computerized financial model that will evaluate the financial
performance of each subsidiary company, and consolidate these results into the holding company. The model
should be flexible and capable of calculating several types of dynamic financial scenarios and tariffs, and should
be able to (i) compute rates of return on rate base and internal rates of return given various levels of loads, tariffs,
O&M costs, fuel costs and amortization; (ii) compute revenue requirements for different returns; (iii) consider
differing borrowing and debt service scenarios; (iv) provide a cash flow analysis; (v) have means of recognizing
local and foreign exchange investments and costs; and (vi) be capable of checking important financial and
operating ratios and guidelines.
(vi)   Formation of Transmission Subsidiary (US$500,000)
As part of its restructuring and privatization program, NPC intends to convert its transmission operations into a
separate subsidiary company in two distinct phases. Phase I would involve forming a separate transmission
profit center within its organization, and transferring the functional responsibility for operation of the
transmission network to this new profit center. NPC envisages work in Phase I to include decisions regarding the
industry and business structure; organizational and staffing requirements and allocations; identification of asset
boundaries and compilation of asset records; review, amendment and implementation of operating procedures;
costs and revenue analysis and budgeting and the preparing of a preliminary business plan. NPC would execute
the work in Phase I with the assistance of consultants.
NPC has asked the Bank is consider providing technical assistance (TA) of about $500,000 equivalent for Phase
II of the exercise, which would involve the actual formation of the transmission subsidiary company. Phase II
would build on the work performed during Phase I, and would involve refining the organizational structure of the
subsidiary; drafting its detailed business plan; recommending technical interfaces with industry participants;
preparing financial projections and capital investment programs; ascertaining funding requirements and
recommending the needed debt/equity mix; developing the regulatory structure in which the subsidiary would
operate; and identifying other actions needed to enable the subsidiary to operate.
2.     Other Technical Assistance Funded by NPC
(i)    Stakeholders analysis - An evaluation of the NPC's Social Development Program - (US$100,000)
Social responsibility dictates that the NPC consider the different stakeholders in policy formulation and program
implementation.  This study shall therefore identify the different stakeholders of NPC and analyze their
relationship with NPC.  It shall also evaluate the existing community relations scheme to determine its
effectiveness and sustainability as a community based development strategy. The TA shall be used to assist in
the conduct of in-house seminar-workshop that will train local personnel in the stakeholder analysis process.
Principles as well as practical learning through case studies, as well as prescriptive tools for managing, will be
discussed. Workshops are focused on experiential learning and surfacing of stakeholder issues confronting the
Corporation. Given the nationwide scope of NPC operations, it shall limit its scope of analysis to the Head
Office and select plants in the three regional centers.
(ii)    Training Programs/Seminars/Workshops/Fact-Finding Missions - (US$ 300.000)
Select groups of NPC staff members will attend training programs/seminars/workshops being conducted by the
International Management Group, Financial Engineering Institute, Euromoney, among others. They will also
participate in fact finding missions, hands-on training, familiarization studies in selected electric utilities which
have undergone restructuring and privatization. The TA will provide them with vital and additional skills



- 86 -                                    Annex 17
Paee 3 of 5
necessary to the various activities involved in the restructuring and privatization program of NPC. Consequently,
these will ensure its smooth, successful and cost-effective implementation.
(iii)   Energy Center Project Study - NPC Efficiency and Reliability Department - (US$400.000)
Energy demand by the year 2005 is estimated to increase to about 16,256 MW with 6.3 M households being
electrified nationwide. NPC's responsibility is to provide information on energy-efficient technologies accessible
through building an Energy Center which will showcase working displays of technologies such as advanced
lighting, air conditioning, glazing, building envelopes and system controls to aid architects, engineers, designers,
owners and developers as well as the household residents. The Center will realize the effectiveness through the
efficient utilization as well as the reduction of electricity consumption nationwide with considerable growth in the
country's GNP. It will also provide an energy resource library to serve as a market of new ideas and information.
The TA will finance consultants to provide the latest information as well as appropriate demonstration
methodology and to determine the energy-saving technologies and/or opportunities to be considered.
(iv)   Integrated Resource Planning Workstation - (US$500,000)
Significant structural changes being considered to the power sector in the Philippines will have profound effect on
the way the system is planned. The planning process has several areas for improvement ranging from
enhancements to the existing legal framework to changes to the specific system planning methods and procedures.
The TA will be used to finance consulting services together with system planning tools and softwares to expand
and enhance the capability of system planners to pursue a more in-depth analysis of least cost system expansion
plan as well as to allow the conduct of more sensitivity studies considering all resources available. A computer
model is required for analyzing bids between competing projects in order to demonstrate and document the factors
prompting the choice for generation additions. Besides being a tool for analyzing competitiveness and economic
value within power pooling environments, the model must also handle all types of thermal, hydro, and renewable
resources as well as all demand-side management programs such as direct load control, efficient lighting
programs and numerous others. It will be used to determine or illustrate the merit of building power generation
facilities to serve export markets or determine the benefits of imports (or establish the price for imports to be
economic).
(v)    Transmission Lines Reliability Improvement Study - (US$600.000)
The project is aimed at assisting NPC identify and determine shortcomings and weaknesses of the current T/L
operations and maintenance practices by conducting a comprehensive review of the existing O/M policies,
procedures, methods, techniques, and technologies being employed. Transmission line reliability is one major
area that is worth looking into with an outside assistance because of its implication on the operational and
financial performance of the Corporation. It is an area where major improvements will be substantiallv rewarded
in terms of savings and reduction in revenue loss due to unplanned line outages. The benefits that will be reaped
from this undertaking are so substantial that even a 50% reduction in unserved energy due to transmission line
outages will lead to the realization of $7.5M in additional revenue over the next five years. The TA will be used
to acquire expert services to look into the current methods, practices and technologies being employed to maintain
and operate our transmission system will give us an opportunity to view the system from the vantage point of an
outsider. The consultant should be able to determine and identify factors which cause unserved energy levels way
beyond our counterpart in other countries. Moreover, he should be able to recommend appropriate solutions that
will result in the reduction of unserved energy to the level of other utilities. The recommended solutions should
also result in the enhancement of the present system as well as the T/L upgrading program under the PDP
masterplan.



- 87 -                                    Annex 17
Page 4 of 5
(vi)   Investor Relations Services - Privatization and Restructuring External Office - (US$3 10.000)
Under this TA, NPC will commission a consulting firm to provide crossborder investor relations services in order
to build the value of its securities that will be sold to the public and thus maximize the proceeds for the
Corporation. While these services will be timed to coincide with the schedule of public securities/offering, other
services such as building NPC's in-house expertise in capital markets by conducting training programs/seminars,
research and identification of opportunities and obstacles related to NPC's public equity and debt securities
offerings, will also be undertaken by the consultant.
(vii)   Property Appraisal and Titling of the Land and Land Rights of NPC - (US$200,000)
NPC presently holds clear titles to only approximately twenty percent of the land it owns. Normally, this would
not present any difficulty to a government corporation. However, with NPC's privatization progran, proper
documentation of its properties becomes necessary. In addition, maintenance of adequate records of these
properties should be developed, specially if it pursues its plan of creating a separate real estate subsidiary not
only to manage these properties but likewise to cievelop the same. The TA will be used to pursue two main
objectives: (1) to have all NPC land and land rights properly surveyed, appraised and titled; and (2) to develop an
adequate record of the land and land rights of NPC. This project shall cover all land and land rights which NPC
owns all over the Philippines. Among the requirements needed in the pursuit of these objectives are the following:
(a) identify, describe, locate and measure the land; (b) determine the more expeditious approach(es) to
obtain titles to the land and land rights and pursue the titling of the same; (c) make an assessment of the
fair value of the land through recognized valuation procedures; (d) develop and maintain a continuous
property record for the land and land rights related to NPC properties.
(viii)  Environmental Management Program - (US$250,000)
Environmental management programs will provide a framework for operating NPC power facilities in
compliance with corporate environmental policies and applicable regulatory requirements. The TA will
provide guidelines for establishing an environmental management program.  It will identify key
components of a comprehensive environmental management program as identified and established by
NPC.  It also will provide human resource requirements which are essential to the effective
implementation of the program.  Although NPC  has established a corporate policy prioritizing
environmental compliance, there are numerous practical reasons for implementing a comprehensive
environmental management program. The program might consist of all or several of the following
components: (a) environmental Management Policies and Programs; (b) minimizing Environmental
Liabilities; (c) emergency Response and Contingency Planning; (d) environmental Auditing
Program/Preparing for ISO 14000. The objectives will be to (a) help NPC recognize and understand the
strategic and operational reasons for implementing an environmental management system; (b) look at the
various tools and approaches NPC can use to develop an environmental management system; (c) identify and
establish attainable goals that are acceptable corporate wide and integrate them into daily operations; (d) ensure
that the Program at a minimum achieves regulatory compliance; (e) create a mechanism or system designed to
control costs of the program; (f) emphasize long range planning versus crisis response; (g) integrate a systems
approach which allows for measurement of Program success
(ix)   Project Management Professional Program for NPC Personnel - (US$300,000)
The objective of this program to be financed under a TA program, is to prepare a select group of Project
Managers (i.e. 10 NPC personnel) in meeting challenges of managing projects, both from within and outside the
organization, using state-of-the-art tools and proven management techniques. The program duration will be three
months at an institute offering training for certification under the US Project Management Institute. The program



- 88 -                                    Annex 17
Paee 5 of 5
will cover the following courses which are deemed relevant to the needs of NPC: Managing Projects in
Organization, Project Leadership, Management & Communications, Telecommunications Principles for Project
Manager, Systems Integration Project Management, Risk Management, Scheduling and Cost Control, Software
Project Management, Construction Project Management, Continuous Improvement and Total Quality Mgmt.,
Software Quality Assurance, Contracting for Project Managers, Project Management Applications, Advance
Topics in Project Management, PMP Certification Exam Preparation, Master's Certificate Exam
